Don't halt the review — recover and keep going.

**When to dig into git history:** if the intent of a modified line is unclear (e.g. you can't tell whether the original behavior was deliberate or accidental, or whether this PR is fixing a regression or introducing one), run `git blame -L <start>,<end> <file>` or `git show <commit-sha>` on the commit that last touched those lines. This is how you separate "author misunderstood an invariant" from "author is changing a documented behavior on purpose."

**Rules for your output:**
1. Read `.codex-scratch/diff.patch` first. Then open the touched files themselves and read enough of them to understand context — call sites, definitions, invariants. Do NOT skim the diff and produce a verdict; a good specialist traces how the changes interact with the rest of the codebase.
2. Focus ONLY on your specialist angle (specified below). Do not duplicate other angles.
3. Output in this exact shape:

```
## [architecture] findings

### Surveyed
- <concrete item, decision, or pattern you examined in this PR> — clean | see Finding N
- <item> — clean | see Finding N
- <item> — clean | see Finding N
(aim for 3–8 bullets, scaled to PR size; this section is how you prove you actually looked rather than skimmed)

### Finding 1 — <severity>
<one paragraph — what is wrong, why it matters, where>
Files: path/to/file.ext:LINE (and additional citations as needed)

### Finding 2 — <severity>
...
```

4. Severity is exactly one of: `blocking`, `medium`, `low`, `nit`. Use `blocking` ONLY for issues that must be fixed before merge.
5. The Surveyed section is REQUIRED even if you have zero findings. A specialist that returns only "No findings" has failed to do its job. If after surveying you genuinely have nothing to raise, output the Surveyed section alone, with each bullet marked `clean` and a brief reason.
6. Be specific. Cite file paths and line numbers. Quote the problematic code in ≤2 lines when it clarifies. **Name the user impact when there is one** — "users retrying a failed payment can be charged twice" beats "this is a race condition." If a finding is purely internal (tech debt, refactoring, DRY), skip the user-impact framing rather than invent one.
7. Keep each finding under 120 words. No preamble, no conclusion, no verdict. The aggregator will assemble the final review.
8. **Remedy-cost framing.** When you raise a finding, name the cost of the remedy you'd propose, not just the LOC delta. The cost is **conditionals + special cases + defensive branches + new abstractions** — LOC is a stand-in for those. The user's standards weight engineer time over compute time, so a remedy that adds N branches for a scenario that doesn't happen is bloat regardless of how the line count nets out. **Don't propose:** defensive guards on internal callers, fallback chains for hypothetical state pollution, type validation outside trust boundaries, wrapper dataclasses for one call site, streaming/incremental rewrites of small in-memory operations on theoretical perf grounds, or extra error handling on fail-fast paths. The test for any edge-case handler: *does the edge case actually happen, or will it in the near future?* If neither, drop the remedy and (depending on whether the underlying finding still stands) downgrade severity or omit the finding. Cite `Concise Code` and `Fail-Fast` from the standards when you flag this in your own output.

**Your angle: Architecture and product strategy.**

FIRST, read `.codex-scratch/product-context.md` in full. The product context tells you the stage of the product, distribution model, and known upcoming roadmap items. Ground your findings in that context.

SECOND, discover and read the repo's own architecture docs before judging architecture. Common locations: `ARCHITECTURE.md`, `docs/architecture/`, `docs/ARCHITECTURE/`, `docs/arc*.md`, `docs/*architecture*.md`, and READMEs in the touched modules. What looks like a bad seam to an outsider is often the documented boundary — and a PR crossing a documented boundary is a stronger finding than one crossing an inferred one. Cite the doc (`docs/architecture/foo.md:LN`) when a finding hinges on it.

Scope:
- **Spirit-vs-implementation.** Read `.codex-scratch/inferred-intent.md`. Then ask: does this implementation deliver on that intent in a way that scales to the next ten variants the user will throw at it, or is it a brittle solution that will need a new branch every time? Look for seams that eliminate special cases and conditional sprawl. Compute cost / latency is an acceptable trade for fewer maintained code paths at this stage. Cite the relevant standards: Fail-Fast, Concise Code, Reframe the Spec, Narrow-Fix.
- Design tradeoffs: did the PR pick an approach that closes off a known roadmap item? (e.g. single-tenant shortcut when multi-tenant is coming)
- Forks in the road: when the PR commits to an architecture (transport, storage, auth, deployment model), note the tradeoff and whether the choice fits the roadmap.
- Lock-in: new external dependencies, new SaaS commitments, new data shapes that will be painful to reverse.
- Layering: violations of existing boundaries (e.g. a handler reaching into a repo layer that was previously isolated).
- Over-engineering for this stage (10 users, moving quickly): excessive abstraction, premature generalization, frameworks where a function would do.
- Under-engineering for imminent needs: hardcoded tenant, global singletons, things the roadmap will force us to refactor within weeks.
- **Cross-cutting patterns introduced in *this* PR**: when the same decision is made across N modules (three parallel changes to three connectors, three new routes with the same shape, three copies of the same guard), flag the layering implication — it usually signals a missing abstraction. The exact code-duplication recommendation belongs to the `simplification` specialist; the seam-bypass diagnosis ("they should have called Config.load, not os.getenv") belongs to the `shape` specialist; you own the architectural framing — why was this the author's only option, and is the missing structure a layer/module-boundary issue rather than a pattern-conformance issue?

Out of scope: specific security bugs, concurrency bugs, test coverage. Also: project-level strict-typing config (mypy/pyright/tsconfig) — the worker runs deterministic per-language checks and auto-posts a `[nit]`; don't double-flag. Type annotations on *individual* new functions remain in your scope when they affect callers' contracts.

Look beyond the diff: grep to understand how the touched modules fit into the broader layering. Read the top-level module structure before making layering claims.

+#!/usr/bin/env bash
+# Mount a Plow DMG and assert it has no custom volume icon (PLO-29 regression
+# guard) and that the volume name is "Plow". Detaches before exiting.
+set -euo pipefail
+
+usage() {
+  cat <<'EOF'
+Usage: plowd-verify-dmg [--dmg <path>]
+
+Mounts the given DMG, asserts the mounted volume is named "Plow" and has no
+.VolumeIcon.icns at its root, then detaches. Defaults to .build/Plow.dmg
+relative to the repo root.
+EOF
+}
+
+repo_root="$(cd "$(dirname "${BASH_SOURCE[0]}")/../../.." && pwd)"
+dmg_path="${repo_root}/.build/Plow.dmg"
+
+while [[ $# -gt 0 ]]; do
+  case "$1" in
+    --dmg)
+      dmg_path="${2:-}"
+      shift 2
+      ;;
+    -h|--help)
+      usage
+      exit 0
+      ;;
+    *)
+      echo "error: unknown argument: $1" >&2
+      usage >&2
+      exit 1
+      ;;
+  esac
+done
+
+if [[ "${dmg_path}" != /* ]]; then
+  dmg_path="${repo_root}/${dmg_path}"
+fi
+
+[[ -f "${dmg_path}" ]] || { echo "error: DMG not found: ${dmg_path}" >&2; exit 1; }
+
+# Refuse to run when a Plow volume is already mounted: the new mountpoint
+# would be "Plow 1" / "Plow 2" / ..., which would mask a real regression in
+# the volume-name assertion below.
+mounted_plow_volumes="$(hdiutil info 2>/dev/null | grep -Eo '/Volumes/Plow( [0-9]+)?$' || true)"
+mounted_plow_volumes="$(printf '%s\n' "${mounted_plow_volumes}" | sort -u)"
+if [[ -n "${mounted_plow_volumes}" ]]; then
+  echo "error: a Plow volume is already mounted; eject it before verifying:" >&2
+  printf '%s\n' "${mounted_plow_volumes}" >&2
+  exit 1
+fi
+
+mounted_volume=""
+cleanup() {
+  local rc=$?
+  if [[ -n "${mounted_volume}" ]]; then
+    if [[ "${rc}" -eq 0 ]]; then
+      # Success path: detach failure (e.g. volume busy) must be fatal.
+      # Otherwise the next release retry trips ensure_no_mounted_plow_volume
+      # in plowd-beta-package-signed and aborts on a leaked mount.
+      if ! hdiutil detach "${mounted_volume}"; then
+        echo "error: failed to detach ${mounted_volume} after successful verify" >&2
+        exit 1
+      fi
+    else
+      # Failure path: don't let detach noise mask the real error.
+      hdiutil detach "${mounted_volume}" >/dev/null 2>&1 || true
+    fi
+  fi
+  exit "${rc}"
+}
+trap cleanup EXIT
+
+attach_output="$(hdiutil attach "${dmg_path}" -nobrowse -readonly)"
+mounted_volume="$(printf '%s\n' "${attach_output}" | sed -n 's|.*\(/Volumes/.*\)$|\1|p' | head -n 1)"
+[[ -n "${mounted_volume}" ]] || { echo "error: failed to mount ${dmg_path}" >&2; exit 1; }
+
+volume_name="$(basename "${mounted_volume}")"
+[[ "${volume_name}" == "Plow" ]] || { echo "error: mounted volume name is '${volume_name}', expected 'Plow'" >&2; exit 1; }
+
+[[ ! -e "${mounted_volume}/.VolumeIcon.icns" ]] || {
+  echo "error: ${mounted_volume}/.VolumeIcon.icns exists; PLO-29 regression: DMG ships a custom volume icon" >&2
+  exit 1
+}
+
+echo "ok: ${dmg_path} mounts as 'Plow' with no custom volume icon"

+@pytest.mark.skipif(platform.system() != "Darwin", reason="hdiutil is macOS-only")
+def test_plowd_verify_dmg_rejects_dmg_shipping_volume_icon(tmp_path):
+    """PLO-29 artifact-level guard. Catches the failure mode that
+    ``test_signed_package_script_builds_ulfo_dmg_without_staging_ds_store``
+    cannot: a regression that re-attaches the DMG post-``hdiutil create``
+    and re-stages a custom volume icon at the final-image stage. We build
+    three real DMGs with hdiutil and assert plowd-verify-dmg accepts the
+    clean one and rejects each regression shape.
+
+    plowd-verify-dmg is wired into plowd-beta-package-signed between staple
+    and S3 upload, so a rejection here aborts ``just release`` before any
+    artifact ships."""
+    # Refuse to run if a real Plow volume is already mounted: the script
+    # bails on that and our assertions would tag the wrong failure mode.
+    info = subprocess.run(
+        ["hdiutil", "info"], capture_output=True, text=True, check=True,
+    )
+    if re.search(r"/Volumes/Plow( [0-9]+)?$", info.stdout, re.MULTILINE):
+        pytest.skip("a Plow volume is mounted; eject it before running this test")
+
+    stage = tmp_path / "stage"
+    (stage / "Plow.app").mkdir(parents=True)
+    (stage / "Plow.app" / "PlaceHolder").write_text("dummy")
+
+    def make_dmg(dmg_path: Path, *, volname: str) -> None:
+        subprocess.run(
+            [
+                "hdiutil", "create",
+                "-volname", volname,
+                "-srcfolder", str(stage),
+                "-ov",
+                "-format", "ULFO",
+                str(dmg_path),
+            ],
+            check=True, capture_output=True,
+        )
+
+    def run_verify(dmg_path: Path) -> subprocess.CompletedProcess[str]:
+        return subprocess.run(
+            [str(VERIFY_DMG_SCRIPT), "--dmg", str(dmg_path)],
+            capture_output=True, text=True,
+        )
+
+    # Happy path: clean Plow DMG with no .VolumeIcon must pass.
+    clean_dmg = tmp_path / "clean.dmg"
+    make_dmg(clean_dmg, volname="Plow")
+    ok = run_verify(clean_dmg)
+    assert ok.returncode == 0, f"clean DMG rejected: stdout={ok.stdout!r} stderr={ok.stderr!r}"
+
+    # Regression #1: someone re-introduces .VolumeIcon.icns at the volume root.
+    (stage / ".VolumeIcon.icns").write_text("fake-icns")
+    iconed_dmg = tmp_path / "iconed.dmg"
+    make_dmg(iconed_dmg, volname="Plow")
+    fail = run_verify(iconed_dmg)
+    assert fail.returncode != 0, "verify-dmg accepted DMG that ships .VolumeIcon.icns"
+    assert ".VolumeIcon.icns exists" in fail.stderr
+
+    # Regression #2: someone parameterizes -volname to something other than "Plow".
+    (stage / ".VolumeIcon.icns").unlink()
+    misnamed_dmg = tmp_path / "misnamed.dmg"
+    make_dmg(misnamed_dmg, volname="NotPlow")
+    fail2 = run_verify(misnamed_dmg)
+    assert fail2.returncode != 0, "verify-dmg accepted DMG with wrong volume name"
+    assert "expected 'Plow'" in fail2.stderr
+
+
+@pytest.mark.skipif(platform.system() != "Darwin", reason="hdiutil is macOS-only")
+def test_plowd_verify_dmg_propagates_detach_failure_on_success_path(tmp_path):
+    """Round-2: if `hdiutil detach` fails on the success path (e.g. the
+    volume is busy), plowd-verify-dmg must exit non-zero. The previous
+    `|| true` swallowed the failure and returned 0, leaking /Volumes/Plow,
+    which then tripped ensure_no_mounted_plow_volume on the next release
+    retry. This test injects an `hdiutil` wrapper whose `detach` always
+    fails and asserts the script surfaces it."""
+    info = subprocess.run(
+        ["hdiutil", "info"], capture_output=True, text=True, check=True,
+    )
+    if re.search(r"/Volumes/Plow( [0-9]+)?$", info.stdout, re.MULTILINE):
+        pytest.skip("a Plow volume is mounted; eject it before running this test")
+
+    stage = tmp_path / "stage"
+    (stage / "Plow.app").mkdir(parents=True)
+    (stage / "Plow.app" / "PlaceHolder").write_text("dummy")
+    dmg = tmp_path / "Plow.dmg"
+    subprocess.run(
+        [
+            "hdiutil", "create",
+            "-volname", "Plow",
+            "-srcfolder", str(stage),
+            "-ov",
+            "-format", "ULFO",
+            str(dmg),
+        ],
+        check=True, capture_output=True,
+    )
+
+    real_hdiutil = subprocess.run(
+        ["which", "hdiutil"], capture_output=True, text=True, check=True,
+    ).stdout.strip()
+    fake_bin = tmp_path / "bin"
+    fake_bin.mkdir()
+    wrapper = fake_bin / "hdiutil"
+    wrapper.write_text(
+        "#!/usr/bin/env bash\n"
+        f'if [[ "$1" == "detach" ]]; then\n'
+        f'  echo "fake: detach failure (test injection)" >&2\n'
+        f'  exit 16\n'
+        f'fi\n'
+        f'exec "{real_hdiutil}" "$@"\n'
+    )
+    wrapper.chmod(0o755)
+
+    try:
+        result = subprocess.run(
+            [str(VERIFY_DMG_SCRIPT), "--dmg", str(dmg)],
+            capture_output=True, text=True,
+            env={
+                **subprocess.os.environ,
+                "PATH": f"{fake_bin}:{subprocess.os.environ['PATH']}",
+            },
+        )
+        assert result.returncode != 0, (
+            f"verify-dmg returned 0 despite detach failure; mount leaked.\n"
+            f"stdout={result.stdout!r}\nstderr={result.stderr!r}"
+        )
+        assert "failed to detach" in result.stderr, (
+            f"expected 'failed to detach' in stderr, got: {result.stderr!r}"
+        )
+    finally:
+        # Real hdiutil to clean up the leaked mount the wrapper refused to release.
+        subprocess.run(
+            [real_hdiutil, "detach", "/Volumes/Plow"],
+            capture_output=True,
+        )
+
+

# Plow

Plow is an agent platform that gives OpenClaw agents narrow, permission-gated access to cloud services (Gmail, Slack) and on-device capabilities through a local approval layer.

The system has three tiers:

- **Plow API** (`api/`) — cloud service that owns connector OAuth, opportunity matching, marketplace skills, and policy enforcement
- **Plow app** (`app/`) — macOS app (Swift) + plowd daemon (Python) that manages on-device approval, gateway configuration, and VM lifecycle
- **Plow CLI** (`cli/`) — narrow tool surface inside the OpenClaw container, talks directly to the Plow API

## Architecture

```mermaid
flowchart TB
    User[User]

    subgraph Mac["macOS Host"]
        Phoenix["Plow.app\n(Swift · Virtualization.framework)"]
        Plowd["plowd daemon\n(:18788 · Python FastAPI)"]

        subgraph VM["Alpine Linux VM"]
            GW["OpenClaw Gateway\n(:18789)"]
            Chan["plow-imessage channel"]
            OC["OpenClaw Agent"]
            CLI["plow CLI\n(containercli)"]
        end
    end

    subgraph Cloud["Cloud (AWS ECS)"]
        API["Plow API\n(FastAPI)"]
        DB["PostgreSQL\n+ pgvector"]
        OE["Opportunity Engine\n(LLM-based JTBD matching)"]

        subgraph Connectors
            GM[Gmail]
            SL[Slack]
        end

        subgraph Channels
            LQ[Linq]
        end
    end

    User --> Phoenix
    Phoenix -->|vsock| VM
    Plowd -->|vsock| VM
    Plowd -->|"gateway operator\n(WebSocket)"| GW
    OC --> CLI
    CLI -->|HTTP| API
    GW --> Chan
    API --> DB
    API --> OE
    API --> GM
    API --> SL
    API --> LQ
```

**Data flow:**

- Inbound SMS → Linq → Plow API webhook → WebSocket → app → LLM → outbound SMS ([full routing doc](docs/architecture/sms-inbound-routing.md))
- `plow gmail search "mortgage"` → CLI → Plow API → Gmail
- `plow slack search "renewal"` → CLI → Plow API → Slack
- OpenClaw never holds raw OAuth tokens — it sees narrow CLI tools only

## Repo Layout

| Directory | Purpose |
|-----------|---------|
| [api/](api/) | Plow API (FastAPI). Connectors in `api/plow/connectors/`, channels in `api/plow/channels/`, opportunity engine in `api/opty_engine/`. |
| [app/](app/) | Plow macOS app (`app/Phoenix/`), plowd daemon (`app/plowd/`), OpenClaw channel plugin (`app/openclaw/`), VM image builder (`app/vm/`). |
| [cli/](cli/) | Plow CLI (containercli). Talks directly to the Plow API via HTTP. |
| [terraform/](terraform/) | AWS infrastructure: ECS, RDS, ALB, VPC, ECR, Secrets Manager. |
| [dtu/](dtu/) | Digital twin units for local testing (e.g., `dtu/linq/` for Linq). |
| [docs/](docs/) | Architecture notes, specs, reports, and spikes. |
| [plow.co/](plow.co/) | Static marketing site deployed on Vercel. |
| [scripts/](scripts/) | Repo-wide utility scripts (e.g., `check_llm_nits.py`). |

## Local Development

The normal local loop is:

1. set up env files
2. boot the API
3. boot the LINQ digital twin
4. build Plow
5. run Plow against the local API

### Prerequisites

- `uv`
- `just`
- Docker Desktop
- Xcode
- macOS for Plow app work

Optional but useful:

- `jq` for inspecting JSON endpoints
- `psql` for local DB inspection
- `npm` if you are changing `app/openclaw/channels/plow-imessage`

### Env files

Each project owns its own env file:

```text
api/.env                 # API runtime config (gitignored) — copy from api/.env.example
api/.env.test-common     # API test defaults (committed)
api/.env.test-live       # API live test creds (gitignored) — copy from api/.env.test-live.example
cli/.env.test-common     # CLI test defaults (committed)
cli/.env.test-live       # CLI live test creds (gitignored) — copy from cli/.env.test-live.example
app/plowd/.env           # Phoenix daemon config (gitignored) — copy from app/plowd/.env.example
dtu/linq/.env            # LINQ twin config (gitignored) — copy from dtu/linq/.env.template
```

### Worktree isolation

`TEST_DB_NAME` is auto-computed from the directory path (`plow_` + 8-char MD5 of the resolved `api/` path). Each checkout/worktree gets a unique test database automatically. CI can override via `TEST_DB_NAME` env var.

For a new worktree:

1. Copy `api/.env.example` to `api/.env`
2. Copy `app/plowd/.env.example` to `app/plowd/.env`
3. Copy `dtu/linq/.env.template` to `dtu/linq/.env`
4. If you want live Gmail or Slack tests, also copy `api/.env.test-live.example` and `cli/.env.test-live.example`

### 1. Set up envs

Create the runtime env files:

```bash
cp api/.env.example api/.env
cp app/plowd/.env.example app/plowd/.env
cp dtu/linq/.env.template dtu/linq/.env
```

`api/.env.example` already defaults LINQ to the local DTU. For most local setups, copying it as-is is enough.

The default local `api/.env` looks like:

```env
DB_HOST=localhost
DB_PORT=55432
DB_NAME=plow
DB_USER=plow
DB_PASSWORD=plow

LINQ_API_KEY=dummy
LINQ_BASE_URL=http://127.0.0.1:8091
LINQ_WEBHOOK_SECRET=test-secret
MANAGED_PHONE=+15550000001

ANTHROPIC_API_KEY=
OAUTH_STATE_SECRET=dev-oauth-state-secret
CORS_ORIGINS='["http://localhost:3000"]'
WEB_BASE_URL=http://localhost:3000
```

Notes:

- LINQ is part of the default local stack. By default the API talks to `dtu/linq`.
- Gmail and Slack OAuth settings are only needed if you want connector flows or live tests.
- `TEST_DB_NAME` is auto-derived for tests. You usually do not need to put it in `api/.env`.
- `just api up` uses the dev DB on port `55432`. The test DB on `55433` is used by test commands.

Minimal `app/plowd/.env` for local app work:

```env
PLOW_API_URL=http://127.0.0.1:8000
```

`dtu/linq/.env` can usually stay close to the template. The important local wiring is:

```env
LINQ_TWIN_PLOW_WEBHOOK_URL=http://127.0.0.1:8000/channels/linq/event
LINQ_TWIN_PLOW_WEBHOOK_SECRET=test-secret
```

If you want live Gmail and Slack tests, also create:

```bash
cp api/.env.test-live.example api/.env.test-live
cp cli/.env.test-live.example cli/.env.test-live
```

### 2. Boot the API

Install Python deps and start the API from the repo root:

```bash
cd api && uv sync
cd ..
just api up
```

What this does:

- starts the shared dev database container if needed
- runs Alembic migrations
- starts the API at `http://127.0.0.1:8000`

Health check:

```bash
curl http://127.0.0.1:8000/health
```

### 3. Boot the LINQ twin

From the repo root:

```bash
cd dtu/linq && just sync
cd ../..
just dtu linq up
```

Then open:

```text

# Plow Mac App

Swift menu bar app that controls PlowD.

## Building from the Command Line

From repo root:

```bash
just app build
just app up
just app release
just app promote
just app logs
```

`just app build` is the app-prep step. It builds the Swift app, stages the PlowD runtime, builds the VM image, and packages the runtime artifacts into the current app variant (`Plow Dev.app` by default).

`just app up` is the fast local launch step. It rebuilds the Swift app, then launches in dev mode against the repo PlowD with hot reload. It still requires a prior `just app build` to seed bundled VM/runtime resources, and again after runtime-facing changes under `app/plowd/`, `app/vm/`, or packaged OpenClaw assets.

`just app release` is the production packaging step. It keeps all outputs under `.build/` and does not touch your local app runtime state in `~/Library/Application Support/...`.

Directly from the app router:

```bash
just app build
just app up
just app release
just app promote
just app logs
```

From `app/` directory:

```bash
cd app

# Full dev prep build (includes VM/runtime packaging)
just build

# Fast dev loop for Swift changes
just up

# Signed release package
just release

# Supporting tools
just logs
```

Build output (including errors) goes to stdout/stderr. The built `.app` bundle lands in the Xcode derived data directory — look for the path in the `BUILD_DIR` line of the output.

## Building from Xcode

```bash
open Phoenix.xcodeproj
```

Then Cmd+R to build and run.

# PlowD

PlowD is the local FastAPI process that manages OpenClaw gateway runtime for the app.

Current scope:

- Start/stop OpenClaw gateway + node host
- Maintain Plow guardrails for `openclaw.json` (loopback + token auth + plugin wiring)
- Run operator WebSocket client for pairing and exec approval decisions
- Expose PlowD status and gateway policy callbacks

Known behaviors and recovery notes:

- historical notes: [`../../docs/openclaw-phoenixd-known-behaviors.md`](../../docs/openclaw-phoenixd-known-behaviors.md)

Script guide:

- [`scripts/README.md`](scripts/README.md)
- [`justfile`](justfile)

## Prerequisites

- `uv`

## Setup

```bash
cd app/plowd
uv sync
cp .env.example .env
```

Edit `.env` as needed for your machine.

## Running

Common rule:

- use the repo root [`justfile`](../../justfile) for normal app workflows
- use the local [`justfile`](justfile) only when you are already working directly inside `app/plowd/`
- the local daemon justfile is intentionally narrow; `just test` is the main supported entrypoint

From repo root:

```bash
just app build
just app up
just app release
just app logs
```

Server:

- `http://127.0.0.1:18788`
- docs: `http://127.0.0.1:18788/docs`

Logs:

- terminal output
- appended to `~/Library/Application Support/co.plow.app/plowd.log`

## Common Workflows

```bash
just app build        # build Swift app + package VM/runtime into the current dev app variant
just app up           # rebuild Swift app, then run against repo PlowD with reload
just app release      # signed release package under .build/
just app logs         # tail app/plowd/vm/openclaw logs
cd app/plowd && just test
cd ../openclaw/channels/plow-imessage && npm run build:watch
```

## Fast Validation Flow

Use `cd app/plowd && just test` for daemon unit coverage.

Use `just app build` once to prepare the app bundle, then `just app up` for the normal local launch loop.

## Active HTTP Surface

- `GET /status`
  - PlowD/gateway/operator readiness
  - includes `agents: {}` for compatibility with existing macOS client contract
- `POST /internal/gateway/policy/tool-check`
- `POST /internal/gateway/policy/tool-result`

# Plow App

The Plow macOS app is currently a local OpenClaw wrapper/orchestrator centered on **PlowD** (the daemon).

## Current Focus

As of this branch, the primary path is:

- PlowD starts and manages OpenClaw gateway + node host locally.
- Plow app tooling keeps app-managed config/state under `~/Library/Application Support/co.plow.app/...` instead of `~/.openclaw/...`.
- Plow gateway policy/operator logic handles pairing and tool approval flows.

The older Wren/Inbox agent-first flow is not the main focus right now, and agent registration on daemon startup is currently disabled.

## Architecture (Now)

- **PlowD (FastAPI daemon)**: process manager + policy service + status API.
- **OpenClaw gateway**: local websocket gateway (`127.0.0.1`, token auth).
- **OpenClaw node host**: execution host process paired to the gateway.
- **OpenClaw dashboard/web chat**: optional local UI client that connects to the same gateway.
- **Plow macOS app**: still exists as iMessage bridge/UI layer, but not the center of this PR.

OpenClaw terms vs app terms:

- PlowD == daemon/operator-side process (not the gateway binary itself)
- OpenClaw gateway == websocket service PlowD launches/manages
- Web client/dashboard == separate operator client that can connect locally when paired/authenticated

State roots are bundle-scoped:

- production app: `~/Library/Application Support/co.plow.app/`
- default dev app: `~/Library/Application Support/co.plow.app.dev/`
- worktree/dev variants: `~/Library/Application Support/<bundle-id>/`

## Quick Start

For the full local stack, use the root [README.md](../README.md). This document stays focused on app-specific details.

1. Set up daemon env:

```bash
cd app/plowd
uv sync
cp .env.example .env
```

2. Fill `app/plowd/.env` with at least:

```env
PLOW_API_URL=http://127.0.0.1:8000
```

3. Build the app bundle and packaged runtime:

```bash
just app build
```

4. Run Plow against the local API:

```bash
just app up
```

## Dev Mode (Fast Iteration)

Use this when you want Python hot reload and live OpenClaw asset edits from the repo:

```bash
just app build
just app up
```

`just app build` prepares the app bundle, including the VM image and packaged runtime. `just app up` is then the normal fast loop for Swift changes: it rebuilds the app and launches with PlowD from `app/plowd/plowd` using `uvicorn --reload`. Run `just app build` again after changes under `app/plowd/`, `app/vm/`, or packaged OpenClaw/runtime assets.

For channel TypeScript edits under `app/openclaw/channels/plow-imessage`:

```bash
cd app/openclaw/channels/plow-imessage && npm run build:watch
```

## Daily Commands

```bash
just app build                     # build Swift app + package VM/runtime into the current dev app variant
just app up
just app release                   # signed release package under .build/

just app logs                      # multiplexed app/PlowD/app-vm/openclaw logs
```

Workflow split:

- run the repo from the root `justfile`
- use `app/justfile` only for local Swift app commands
- use `app/plowd/justfile` only for local daemon tests and internal maintenance; the supported app workflows are the `just app ...` commands above

## Code Signing

Local app builds are signed by default with the shared Apple team configured in [`app/Phoenix/Config/App.xcconfig`](../app/Phoenix/Config/App.xcconfig). That keeps dev builds closer to production identity and is the preferred path for avoiding repeated Full Disk Access prompts during normal rebuilds.

For release notarization setup and the personal-team override path, see [`docs/distribution/CODE_SIGNING.md`](distribution/CODE_SIGNING.md).

## State Boundaries (Avoiding Sprawl)

OpenClaw runs inside a VM sandbox managed by PlowD. All state is pinned to app-managed paths under `~/Library/Application Support/<bundle-id>/`:

- config: `~/Library/Application Support/<bundle-id>/openclaw/gateway/openclaw.json`
- state: `~/Library/Application Support/<bundle-id>/openclaw/gateway`
- token: `~/Library/Application Support/<bundle-id>/openclaw/secrets/gateway-token`

Reference and recovery notes:

- [plowd/README.md](../app/plowd/README.md)
- [openclaw-phoenixd-known-behaviors.md](openclaw-phoenixd-known-behaviors.md)

## macOS Layer (Still Present)

The Swift app in `app/` still provides the iMessage bridge (`chat.db` clone to `~/Library/Application Support/<bundle-id>/imessage/chat_clone.db`) and local UI controls. `app/plowd/` is the host daemon/runtime. That layer remains part of the Plow app, but this PR/workstream is primarily about stable OpenClaw gateway integration through PlowD.

## Repository Layout

```
plow/
├── api/                  # Plow cloud API (FastAPI, SQLAlchemy, connectors)
├── app/                  # Swift app, PlowD daemon, OpenClaw assets, VM
│   ├── Phoenix/          # Swift macOS app
│   ├── plowd/            # Python FastAPI daemon
│   ├── openclaw/         # Channel plugins (plow-imessage)
│   └── vm/               # VM sandbox: rootfs build, kernel, init scripts
├── cli/                  # Plow CLI (runs inside OpenClaw container)
├── dtu/                  # Digital twin units for local testing
├── docs/                 # Architecture docs, spikes, distribution guides
└── justfile              # Primary command entrypoints
```

# File Taxonomy: Upstream vs Wrapper vs User State vs Team-Tracked

*Last updated: 2026-04-29*

Every file in the Plow universe belongs to exactly one of four categories.
Mixing them is the source of nearly every "broken on upgrade" or "shipped
user data" incident we hit.

The pre-commit guard at `scripts/check_protected_paths.py` enforces the rules
below by blocking edits to known protected paths; overrides are possible but
intentional.

## The four categories

| # | Category | Source of truth | On user's disk at runtime | Who modifies | Modify directly? |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| **(a)** | **Upstream OpenClaw runtime** — Gateway, ACP runner, cron engine, heartbeat loop, plugin SDK, Control UI | `openclaw/upstream` repo (NOT in this tree); pulled at VM build time via `npm install -g openclaw@<version>` (pinned in `app/vm/manifest.toml`) | Inside the Lima VM's OCI image at `/usr/local/lib/node_modules/openclaw/`. Never on the host FS. | Upstream maintainers | **No.** Any host-side edit is overwritten on the next VM image pull. Fix behavior in (b), or open a PR upstream and bump the pin. |
| **(b)** | **Plow wrapper code** that we author and ship | This repo: `app/Phoenix/` (Swift app), `app/plowd/plowd/` (Python daemon), `app/openclaw/plugins/{guard,plow-cli}/`, `app/openclaw/channels/plow-imessage/`, `app/openclaw/templates/workspace/`, `app/openclaw/marketplace/`, `app/vm/`, `api/plow/`, `cli/` | Packaged into `Plow.app/Contents/Resources/runtime/…` at build time | Plow engineers (us) via PR | **Yes** — this is the only layer we own. All fixes, features, new tools, guardrail changes belong here. |
| **(c)** | **Per-install user state** — per-machine config, history, secrets, workspace | Written at runtime by Plow or by the user; *never* committed to this repo | `~/Library/Application Support/co.plow.app/openclaw/…` (prod), `…/co.plow.app.dev.wt1/…` (dev variants), `~/.openclaw/` (standalone dev installs), `~/Plow/` (user's shared workspace folder), `~/.phoenix/` (PhoenixD state) | The running Plow app, or the user | **Rarely.** Only: (i) live-debugging *this* machine with explicit consent, (ii) a one-time first-launch migration written as (b) code, (iii) (b) code seeding defaults into fresh (c) state (e.g. `plowd/gateway.py::_apply_locked_guardrails`). Never check (c) data into the repo; never rely on a manual (c) edit to persist a behavior change. |
| **(d)** | **Team-tracked skill bundles** — opt-in skill bundles the team wants under git for review and history but explicitly NOT default-shipped. Currently `team-skills/`. Distinct from `app/openclaw/marketplace/` (which is (b) and ships with Plow.app). | This repo: `team-skills/` | Nowhere by default. Users who want a bundle copy or reference it into their own `/workspace/skills/` manually. | Plow engineers (us) via PR | **Yes** — same review process as (b), but no build/install pipeline picks (d) up automatically. The `skill-install-state` guard rule blocks (c) install metadata (`.clawhub/`, `_meta.json`) from leaking into `(d)` when copying a live skill. |

## VM recreate safety

The Lima VM can be destroyed and recreated without losing any user data.
All (c) state is on the host and mounted into the VM via virtiofs — confirmed
in `app/vm/lima.yaml`:

| Mount point | Host location placeholder | Writable | Category |
|---|---|---|---|
| `/workspace` | `__PLOW_WORKSPACE_DIR__` | yes | (c) user workspace |
| `/config` | `__PLOW_CONFIG_DIR__` | yes | (c) per-install config |
| `/mounts` | `__PLOW_MOUNTS_DIR__` | yes | (c) user-attached mounts |
| `/vm-logs` | `__PLOW_VM_LOGS_DIR__` | yes | (c) runtime logs |
| `/plugin`, `/plow-cli-plugin`, `/plow-imessage`, `/cli-packages`, `/images` | various | **no** | (b) shipped code, read-only |

Nothing user-valuable lives only inside the VM filesystem. The read-only
mounts are all (b) code that Phoenix re-provides from `Plow.app` on the next
launch. A `limactl delete` + re-provision is therefore safe at any time.

## Two rules that follow from the taxonomy

### Rule 1 — Never ship (c) data

Anything that ends up in `Plow.app/Contents/Resources/` must be (b) content.
Two paths cross the boundary and need the most vigilance:

1. **`app/openclaw/templates/workspace/`** — files here are copied into each
   user's fresh (c) workspace on first run. They must remain generic
   skeletons. Personalized variants (`HEARTBEAT.md`, populated `USER.md`)
   belong in (c), not (b).

2. **`app/openclaw/marketplace/`** — shipped cron recipes / skill bundles
   users can instantiate. Same rule: generic, no personal data.

### Rule 2 — Never modify (a)

There is no (a) source in this repo. The surface area for accidentally
"patching upstream" is at runtime on a dev's machine:

- `~/Library/Application Support/co.plow.app/openclaw/gateway/openclaw.json` —
  your personal generated config. Host-side edits are overwritten next
  launch by `plowd/gateway.py::_apply_locked_guardrails`. To change defaults,
  edit the generator in (b).
- `~/.openclaw/` — same pattern for the standalone dev install.
- `/usr/local/lib/node_modules/openclaw/` inside the VM — replaced on every
  VM image pull.

If you keep needing to make the same manual edit in (c), that's a missing
(b) feature. File it, don't repeat it.

## The protected-paths guard

`scripts/check_protected_paths.py` is wired into `.pre-commit-config.yaml` as
the `check-protected-paths` hook. It inspects each staged file against a
short list of rules; each rule has a stable `id` that can be used to
override the check for a single commit.

### Rule types

Two mechanisms work in parallel:

**Path-based rules** (`RULES` in `scripts/check_protected_paths.py`) block a
file from being staged at all when its path matches a glob. Override per
commit with `PLOW_GUARD_ALLOW=<rule-id>`.

**Skeleton-drift check** (`scripts/protected-skeleton-hashes.txt`) pins a
SHA256 for each shipped-skeleton file. Any modification that doesn't match
the pinned hash fails the check. There is **no** `PLOW_GUARD_ALLOW` for
drift on purpose: updating the pinned hash in the same commit *is* the
override, and it's visible to reviewers in the diff.

### Current rules

| `id` | Kind | Patterns / pin | Category | Override |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `user-state` | path | `**/cron/jobs.json`, `**/cron/jobs.json.*`, `**/cron/runs/*.jsonl`, `**/sessions/store.json`, `**/agents/*/sessions/*.jsonl`, `**/gateway-token`, `**/node-device-id`, `**/plow-api-token`, `**/plow-local-token` | (c) per-machine runtime state | `PLOW_GUARD_ALLOW=user-state` |
| `personal-workspace-file` | path | `app/openclaw/templates/workspace/HEARTBEAT.md` | (b)→(c) personalized template | `PLOW_GUARD_ALLOW=personal-workspace-file` |
| `openclaw-upstream-pin` | path | `app/vm/manifest.toml` | (a) upstream version pin | `PLOW_GUARD_ALLOW=openclaw-upstream-pin` |
| `skill-install-state` | path | `**/.clawhub/**`, `team-skills/**/_meta.json` | (c) per-install skill metadata leaking into the repo | `PLOW_GUARD_ALLOW=skill-install-state` |
| `skeleton-drift` | hash | `app/openclaw/templates/workspace/USER.md`, `…/IDENTITY.md` | (b) canonical shipped skeleton | Update pin in `scripts/protected-skeleton-hashes.txt` in the same commit |

### Overriding a path rule for a single commit

When an edit is intentional — e.g. bumping the upstream pin after a
release, or force-adding `HEARTBEAT.md` for some legit reason:

```bash
PLOW_GUARD_ALLOW=openclaw-upstream-pin git commit -m "vm: bump openclaw to 2026.5.1"
PLOW_GUARD_ALLOW=personal-workspace-file,openclaw-upstream-pin git commit ...
```

Overrides are per-invocation; there is no persistent allow-list file on
purpose — the override should appear explicitly in the shell history and be
visible to reviewers via the commit's scope.

### Updating a pinned skeleton

You intentionally changed `USER.md` or `IDENTITY.md` in a way every Plow
user should see. To ship it:

```bash
# 1. Make your edit to the skeleton file.
# 2. Get the new hash.
shasum -a 256 app/openclaw/templates/workspace/USER.md
# 3. Update the matching line in scripts/protected-skeleton-hashes.txt
# 4. Stage both files and commit.
git add app/openclaw/templates/workspace/USER.md scripts/protected-skeleton-hashes.txt
git commit -m "templates(workspace): add <field> to USER.md skeleton"
```

The guard will pass because the recomputed SHA matches the new pin. The
diff on `scripts/protected-skeleton-hashes.txt` makes the intent explicit
to reviewers and forces a moment of reflection per this doc — that's the
entire point.

### Adding a new rule

**New path rule:** edit the `RULES` list in
`scripts/check_protected_paths.py` and add a row to the table above.
Fields: `id` (short kebab-case token), `category` (string tag), `patterns`
(glob list), `why` (failure message). Glob dialect: `**` (any number of
path components), `*` (non-slash chars), `?` (one non-slash char);
everything else literal.

**New skeleton pin:** add a line to
`scripts/protected-skeleton-hashes.txt` with the file's current SHA256 and
its repo-relative path, then add it to the table above.

   248	  codesign --verify --deep --strict --verbose=4 "${preserved_app}"
   249	  echo "preserved signed app for inspection: ${preserved_app}"
   250	fi
   251	
   252	"${stage_sparkle_script}" \
   253	  --app-bundle "${stage_app}" \
   254	  --archives-dir "${sparkle_stage_dir}" \
   255	  --download-url-prefix "${sparkle_download_url_prefix}" \
   256	  --account "${sparkle_account}"
   257	
   258	rm -f "${output}" "${output}.sha256"
   259	echo "creating DMG..."
   260	hdiutil create \
   261	  -volname "Plow" \
   262	  -srcfolder "${stage_dir}" \
   263	  -ov \
   264	  -format ULFO \
   265	  "${output}"
   266

   268	attach_output="$(hdiutil attach "${output}" -nobrowse)"
   269	mounted_volume="$(printf '%s\n' "${attach_output}" | sed -n 's|.*\(/Volumes/.*\)$|\1|p' | head -n 1)"
   270	[[ -n "${mounted_volume}" ]] || { echo "error: failed to determine mounted volume for ${output}" >&2; exit 1; }
   271	codesign --verify --deep --strict --verbose=4 "${mounted_volume}/Plow.app"
   272	hdiutil detach "${mounted_volume}" >/dev/null
   273	mounted_volume=""
   274	
   275	echo "submitting DMG to Apple notarization..."
   276	submit_output="$(xcrun notarytool submit "${output}" --keychain-profile "${notary_profile}" --wait --output-format json)"
   277	submit_id="$(python3 -c 'import json,sys; print(json.load(sys.stdin).get("id",""))' <<<"${submit_output}")"
   278	submit_status="$(python3 -c 'import json,sys; print(json.load(sys.stdin).get("status",""))' <<<"${submit_output}")"
   279	if [[ "${submit_status}" != "Accepted" ]]; then
   280	  echo "notarization failed with status: ${submit_status:-unknown}" >&2
   281	  if [[ -n "${submit_id}" ]]; then
   282	    echo "submission id: ${submit_id}" >&2
   283	    xcrun notarytool log "${submit_id}" --keychain-profile "${notary_profile}" || true
   284	  fi
   285	  exit 1
   286	fi
   287	echo "stapling notarization ticket..."
   288	xcrun stapler staple "${output}"
   289	echo "checking local Gatekeeper assessment for the DMG..."
   290	if ! spctl --assess --type open -vv "${output}"; then
   291	  echo "warning: local spctl assessment of the DMG failed; notarization was accepted and the ticket was stapled" >&2
   292	fi
   293	
   294	# PLO-29: verify the final shipping artifact has no custom volume icon and
   295	# that the volume name is "Plow" before it gets uploaded. plowd-verify-dmg
   296	# performs a real `hdiutil attach` of the stapled DMG, so this can only run
   297	# against a real filesystem; the unit-test path that stubs hdiutil sets

   301	  "${repo_root}/app/plowd/scripts/plowd-verify-dmg" --dmg "${output}"
   302	fi
   303

   305	shasum -a 256 "${output}" > "${output}.sha256"
   306	
   307	echo "signed distribution image created: ${output}"
   308	echo "sha256 file: ${output}.sha256"
   309	profile_args=()
   310	if [[ -n "${s3_profile}" ]]; then
   311	  profile_args=(--profile "${s3_profile}")
   312	fi

 succeeded in 0ms:
     1	#!/usr/bin/env bash
     2	# Mount a Plow DMG and assert it has no custom volume icon (PLO-29 regression
     3	# guard) and that the volume name is "Plow". Detaches before exiting.
     4	set -euo pipefail
     5	
     6	usage() {
     7	  cat <<'EOF'
     8	Usage: plowd-verify-dmg [--dmg <path>]
     9	
    10	Mounts the given DMG, asserts the mounted volume is named "Plow" and has no
    11	.VolumeIcon.icns at its root, then detaches. Defaults to .build/Plow.dmg
    12	relative to the repo root.
    13	EOF
    14	}
    15	
    16	repo_root="$(cd "$(dirname "${BASH_SOURCE[0]}")/../../.." && pwd)"
    17	dmg_path="${repo_root}/.build/Plow.dmg"
    18	
    19	while [[ $# -gt 0 ]]; do
    20	  case "$1" in
    21	    --dmg)
    22	      dmg_path="${2:-}"
    23	      shift 2
    24	      ;;
    25	    -h|--help)
    26	      usage
    27	      exit 0
    28	      ;;
    29	    *)
    30	      echo "error: unknown argument: $1" >&2
    31	      usage >&2
    32	      exit 1
    33	      ;;
    34	  esac
    35	done
    36	
    37	if [[ "${dmg_path}" != /* ]]; then
    38	  dmg_path="${repo_root}/${dmg_path}"
    39	fi
    40	
    41	[[ -f "${dmg_path}" ]] || { echo "error: DMG not found: ${dmg_path}" >&2; exit 1; }
    42	
    43	# Refuse to run when a Plow volume is already mounted: the new mountpoint
    44	# would be "Plow 1" / "Plow 2" / ..., which would mask a real regression in
    45	# the volume-name assertion below.
    46	mounted_plow_volumes="$(hdiutil info 2>/dev/null | grep -Eo '/Volumes/Plow( [0-9]+)?$' || true)"
    47	mounted_plow_volumes="$(printf '%s\n' "${mounted_plow_volumes}" | sort -u)"
    48	if [[ -n "${mounted_plow_volumes}" ]]; then
    49	  echo "error: a Plow volume is already mounted; eject it before verifying:" >&2
    50	  printf '%s\n' "${mounted_plow_volumes}" >&2
    51	  exit 1
    52	fi
    53	
    54	mounted_volume=""
    55	cleanup() {
    56	  local rc=$?
    57	  if [[ -n "${mounted_volume}" ]]; then
    58	    if [[ "${rc}" -eq 0 ]]; then
    59	      # Success path: detach failure (e.g. volume busy) must be fatal.
    60	      # Otherwise the next release retry trips ensure_no_mounted_plow_volume
    61	      # in plowd-beta-package-signed and aborts on a leaked mount.
    62	      if ! hdiutil detach "${mounted_volume}"; then
    63	        echo "error: failed to detach ${mounted_volume} after successful verify" >&2
    64	        exit 1
    65	      fi
    66	    else
    67	      # Failure path: don't let detach noise mask the real error.
    68	      hdiutil detach "${mounted_volume}" >/dev/null 2>&1 || true
    69	    fi
    70	  fi
    71	  exit "${rc}"
    72	}
    73	trap cleanup EXIT
    74	
    75	attach_output="$(hdiutil attach "${dmg_path}" -nobrowse -readonly)"
    76	mounted_volume="$(printf '%s\n' "${attach_output}" | sed -n 's|.*\(/Volumes/.*\)$|\1|p' | head -n 1)"
    77	[[ -n "${mounted_volume}" ]] || { echo "error: failed to mount ${dmg_path}" >&2; exit 1; }
    78	
    79	volume_name="$(basename "${mounted_volume}")"
    80	[[ "${volume_name}" == "Plow" ]] || { echo "error: mounted volume name is '${volume_name}', expected 'Plow'" >&2; exit 1; }
    81	
    82	[[ ! -e "${mounted_volume}/.VolumeIcon.icns" ]] || {
    83	  echo "error: ${mounted_volume}/.VolumeIcon.icns exists; PLO-29 regression: DMG ships a custom volume icon" >&2
    84	  exit 1
    85	}
    86	
    87	echo "ok: ${dmg_path} mounts as 'Plow' with no custom volume icon"

    20	def _provision_fake_bin(fake_bin: Path, systemctl_log: Path) -> None:
    21	    """Write stub commands sufficient to run provision-runtime.sh on macOS."""
    22	    stubs = {
    23	        # zstd just needs to be on PATH so the apt-get install branch is skipped
    24	        "zstd": "#!/bin/sh\n",
    25	        # sha256sum: hash stdin or file args, mimicking GNU coreutils behaviour
    26	        "sha256sum": textwrap.dedent("""\
    27	            #!/usr/bin/env python3
    28	            import hashlib, sys
    29	            from pathlib import Path
    30	            args = [a for a in sys.argv[1:] if a != "--"]
    31	            if args:
    32	                for arg in args:
    33	                    try:
    34	                        data = Path(arg).read_bytes()
    35	                        print(hashlib.sha256(data).hexdigest() + "  " + arg)
    36	                    except FileNotFoundError:
    37	                        print(f"sha256sum: {arg}: No such file or directory", file=sys.stderr)
    38	                        sys.exit(1)
    39	            else:
    40	                data = sys.stdin.buffer.read()
    41	                print(hashlib.sha256(data).hexdigest() + "  -")
    42	            """),
    43	        # systemctl: log every invocation; always succeed
    44	        "systemctl": f'#!/bin/sh\necho "$@" >> "{systemctl_log}"\n',
    45	    }
    46	    for name, body in stubs.items():
    47	        p = fake_bin / name
    48	        p.write_text(body)
    49	        p.chmod(0o755)
    50

    53	    unit_dir = tmp_path / "units"

    55	    libexec_dir = tmp_path / "libexec"

    57	    return subprocess.run(
    58	        ["bash", str(PROVISION_SCRIPT)],

    60	        text=True,
    61	        env={
    62	            **subprocess.os.environ,

    64	            "PLOW_UNIT_DIR": str(unit_dir),
    65	            "PLOW_LIBEXEC_DIR": str(libexec_dir),
    66	        },
    67	    )

    70	def test_provision_restarts_containerd_on_first_run(tmp_path):
    71	    """containerd.service is restarted when unit files are written for the first time."""
    72	    fake_bin = tmp_path / "bin"

    84	def test_provision_skips_containerd_restart_when_units_unchanged(tmp_path):
    85	    """containerd.service is not restarted when provision writes identical unit files."""
    86	    fake_bin = tmp_path / "bin"

    89	    _provision_fake_bin(fake_bin, systemctl_log)
    90

    92	    r1 = _run_provision(tmp_path, fake_bin)
    93	    assert r1.returncode == 0, r1.stderr
    94	
    95	    # Second run — same unit content; containerd restart must be skipped
    96	    systemctl_log.unlink()
    97	    r2 = _run_provision(tmp_path, fake_bin)
    98	    assert r2.returncode == 0, r2.stderr
    99	
   100	    calls = systemctl_log.read_text().splitlines() if systemctl_log.exists() else []
   101	    assert not any("restart containerd.service" in c for c in calls), (
   102	        f"containerd was restarted on unchanged provision run:\n" + "\n".join(calls)
   103	    )

   192	    _write_fake_release_commands(fake_bin)
   193	
   194	    env = {

   196	        "PATH": f"{fake_bin}:{subprocess.os.environ['PATH']}",

   199	        "SPARKLE_BIN_DIR": str(fake_bin),
   200	        # PLO-29: the post-staple verify needs a real hdiutil mount; under
   201	        # stubbed hdiutil it can't actually attach the fake DMG, so skip.
   202	        # The artifact-level guard is exercised by
   203	        # test_plowd_verify_dmg_rejects_dmg_shipping_volume_icon.
   204	        "PLOW_SKIP_DMG_VERIFY": "1",
   205	    }
   206	
   207	    result = subprocess.run(
   208	        [
   209	            str(SIGNED_PACKAGE_SCRIPT),
   210	            "--app-bundle",

   212	            "--output",
   213	            str(output),

   215	            "Developer ID Application: Example (3559PD337Z)",
   216	            "--notary-profile",
   217	            "test-notary",
   218	            "--s3-bucket",
   219	            "test-bucket",
   220	            "--release-prefix",
   221	            "beta",
   222	            "--s3-profile",
   223	            "test-profile",
   224	        ],
   225	        capture_output=True,
   226	        text=True,
   227	        cwd=REPO_ROOT,
   228	        env=env,
   229	    )

   236	    assert "-format ULFO" in hdiutil_log
   237	    # PLO-29: DMG is created directly as ULFO; the old UDRW->convert dance
   238	    # only existed to host a kHasCustomIcon FinderInfo write on a mounted

   246	    assert not (staged_dir / ".DS_Store").exists()

   248	    # PLO-29: the mounted volume must show the default macOS volume icon,
   249	    # so the staged srcfolder must not ship a .VolumeIcon.icns.
   250	    assert not (staged_dir / ".VolumeIcon.icns").exists()
   251	    assert not (staged_dir / "Plow-rw.dmg").exists()

   254	@pytest.mark.skipif(platform.system() != "Darwin", reason="hdiutil is macOS-only")
   255	def test_plowd_verify_dmg_rejects_dmg_shipping_volume_icon(tmp_path):
   256	    """PLO-29 artifact-level guard. Catches the failure mode that
   257	    ``test_signed_package_script_builds_ulfo_dmg_without_staging_ds_store``
   258	    cannot: a regression that re-attaches the DMG post-``hdiutil create``
   259	    and re-stages a custom volume icon at the final-image stage. We build
   260	    three real DMGs with hdiutil and assert plowd-verify-dmg accepts the
   261	    clean one and rejects each regression shape.
   262	
   263	    plowd-verify-dmg is wired into plowd-beta-package-signed between staple
   264	    and S3 upload, so a rejection here aborts ``just release`` before any
   265	    artifact ships."""
   266	    # Refuse to run if a real Plow volume is already mounted: the script
   267	    # bails on that and our assertions would tag the wrong failure mode.
   268	    info = subprocess.run(
   269	        ["hdiutil", "info"], capture_output=True, text=True, check=True,
   270	    )
   271	    if re.search(r"/Volumes/Plow( [0-9]+)?$", info.stdout, re.MULTILINE):
   272	        pytest.skip("a Plow volume is mounted; eject it before running this test")
   273	
   274	    stage = tmp_path / "stage"
   275	    (stage / "Plow.app").mkdir(parents=True)
   276	    (stage / "Plow.app" / "PlaceHolder").write_text("dummy")
   277	
   278	    def make_dmg(dmg_path: Path, *, volname: str) -> None:
   279	        subprocess.run(
   280	            [
   281	                "hdiutil", "create",
   282	                "-volname", volname,
   283	                "-srcfolder", str(stage),
   284	                "-ov",
   285	                "-format", "ULFO",
   286	                str(dmg_path),
   287	            ],
   288	            check=True, capture_output=True,
   289	        )
   290	
   291	    def run_verify(dmg_path: Path) -> subprocess.CompletedProcess[str]:
   292	        return subprocess.run(
   293	            [str(VERIFY_DMG_SCRIPT), "--dmg", str(dmg_path)],
   294	            capture_output=True, text=True,
   295	        )
   296	
   297	    # Happy path: clean Plow DMG with no .VolumeIcon must pass.
   298	    clean_dmg = tmp_path / "clean.dmg"
   299	    make_dmg(clean_dmg, volname="Plow")
   300	    ok = run_verify(clean_dmg)
   301	    assert ok.returncode == 0, f"clean DMG rejected: stdout={ok.stdout!r} stderr={ok.stderr!r}"
   302	
   303	    # Regression #1: someone re-introduces .VolumeIcon.icns at the volume root.
   304	    (stage / ".VolumeIcon.icns").write_text("fake-icns")
   305	    iconed_dmg = tmp_path / "iconed.dmg"
   306	    make_dmg(iconed_dmg, volname="Plow")
   307	    fail = run_verify(iconed_dmg)
   308	    assert fail.returncode != 0, "verify-dmg accepted DMG that ships .VolumeIcon.icns"
   309	    assert ".VolumeIcon.icns exists" in fail.stderr
   310	
   311	    # Regression #2: someone parameterizes -volname to something other than "Plow".
   312	    (stage / ".VolumeIcon.icns").unlink()
   313	    misnamed_dmg = tmp_path / "misnamed.dmg"
   314	    make_dmg(misnamed_dmg, volname="NotPlow")
   315	    fail2 = run_verify(misnamed_dmg)
   316	    assert fail2.returncode != 0, "verify-dmg accepted DMG with wrong volume name"
   317	    assert "expected 'Plow'" in fail2.stderr
   318	
   319	
   320	@pytest.mark.skipif(platform.system() != "Darwin", reason="hdiutil is macOS-only")
   321	def test_plowd_verify_dmg_propagates_detach_failure_on_success_path(tmp_path):
   322	    """Round-2: if `hdiutil detach` fails on the success path (e.g. the
   323	    volume is busy), plowd-verify-dmg must exit non-zero. The previous
   324	    `|| true` swallowed the failure and returned 0, leaking /Volumes/Plow,
   325	    which then tripped ensure_no_mounted_plow_volume on the next release
   326	    retry. This test injects an `hdiutil` wrapper whose `detach` always
   327	    fails and asserts the script surfaces it."""
   328	    info = subprocess.run(
   329	        ["hdiutil", "info"], capture_output=True, text=True, check=True,
   330	    )
   331	    if re.search(r"/Volumes/Plow( [0-9]+)?$", info.stdout, re.MULTILINE):
   332	        pytest.skip("a Plow volume is mounted; eject it before running this test")
   333	
   334	    stage = tmp_path / "stage"
   335	    (stage / "Plow.app").mkdir(parents=True)
   336	    (stage / "Plow.app" / "PlaceHolder").write_text("dummy")
   337	    dmg = tmp_path / "Plow.dmg"
   338	    subprocess.run(
   339	        [
   340	            "hdiutil", "create",
   341	            "-volname", "Plow",
   342	            "-srcfolder", str(stage),
   343	            "-ov",
   344	            "-format", "ULFO",
   345	            str(dmg),
   346	        ],
   347	        check=True, capture_output=True,
   348	    )
   349	
   350	    real_hdiutil = subprocess.run(
   351	        ["which", "hdiutil"], capture_output=True, text=True, check=True,
   352	    ).stdout.strip()
   353	    fake_bin = tmp_path / "bin"
   354	    fake_bin.mkdir()
   355	    wrapper = fake_bin / "hdiutil"
   356	    wrapper.write_text(
   357	        "#!/usr/bin/env bash\n"
   358	        f'if [[ "$1" == "detach" ]]; then\n'
   359	        f'  echo "fake: detach failure (test injection)" >&2\n'
   360	        f'  exit 16\n'
   361	        f'fi\n'
   362	        f'exec "{real_hdiutil}" "$@"\n'
   363	    )
   364	    wrapper.chmod(0o755)
   365	
   366	    try:
   367	        result = subprocess.run(
   368	            [str(VERIFY_DMG_SCRIPT), "--dmg", str(dmg)],
   369	            capture_output=True, text=True,
   370	            env={
   371	                **subprocess.os.environ,
   372	                "PATH": f"{fake_bin}:{subprocess.os.environ['PATH']}",
   373	            },
   374	        )
   375	        assert result.returncode != 0, (
   376	            f"verify-dmg returned 0 despite detach failure; mount leaked.\n"
   377	            f"stdout={result.stdout!r}\nstderr={result.stderr!r}"
   378	        )
   379	        assert "failed to detach" in result.stderr, (
   380	            f"expected 'failed to detach' in stderr, got: {result.stderr!r}"

exec

 succeeded in 0ms:
# `app/plowd/scripts` Guide

These scripts are the supported CLI entrypoints for Plow packaged runtime workflows.
Prefer `just app ...` routers from repo root where possible.

## Active Scripts

- `plowd-package-runtime`
  - Syncs a staged runtime payload into `Plow.app`.
  - Intended for local packaging/release assembly workflows.

- `plowd-package-sparkle-update`
  - Archives a signed `Plow.app` into a Sparkle-friendly ZIP update artifact.
  - Use after the final app bundle has been signed.

- `plowd-stage-sparkle-feed`
  - Packages a `Plow.app` bundle and generates a local `appcast.xml`.
  - Use this to stage a non-prod or prod Sparkle feed directory before upload.

- `plowd-publish-sparkle-feed`
  - Publishes a staged Sparkle feed to explicit S3 keys without deleting unrelated files.
  - Used for production appcast/archive uploads.

- `plowd-promote-release`
  - Promotes a versioned release to the stable DMG and appcast keys.
  - Use this after validation to make a packaged release visible to users.

- `plowd-stage-runtime`
  - Assembles bundled runtime under `app/plowd/runtime/stage`.
  - Installs pinned Python + locked PlowD deps + stages OpenClaw assets from `app/openclaw/`.

- `plowd-fetch-runtime-artifacts`
  - Downloads pinned Node/OpenClaw artifacts into `app/plowd/runtime/artifacts`.
  - Can write SHA256 values back into `app/plowd/runtime/manifest.toml`.

- `plowd-validate-package`
  - Validates packaged runtime end-to-end (`offline` or `online` mode).
  - Checks bundle layout, launch source, and bundled CLI wiring.

- `plowd-packaged-agent`
  - Runs bundled OpenClaw CLI from a packaged `Plow.app`.
  - Requires `PLOWD_OPENCLAW_ROOT_DIR` to point at the active bundle-scoped OpenClaw root, for example `~/Library/Application Support/<bundle-id>/openclaw`.

- `plowd-tail-logs`
  - Tails app/plowd/vm/openclaw logs with source filtering and timestamps.

## Removed From This Folder

PoC utilities were removed from `app/plowd/scripts` because they are not part of
the current supported flow and are not called by the root `justfile` or PlowD runtime.

Historical PoC copies remain under:

- `spikes/openclaw-integration/`
- `spikes/openclaw-production-architecture/`

   517	def _create_minimal_valid_app_bundle(app_bundle: Path) -> None:
   518	    contents_root = app_bundle / "Contents"
   519	    macos_root = contents_root / "MacOS"
   520	    runtime_root = app_bundle / "Contents" / "Resources" / "runtime"
   521	    vm_root = app_bundle / "Contents" / "Resources" / "vm"
   522	    info_plist = contents_root / "Info.plist"
   523	    macos_binary = macos_root / "Plow"
   524	    macos_root.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
   525	    info_plist.write_text(
   526	        """<?xml version="1.0" encoding="UTF-8"?>
   527	<!DOCTYPE plist PUBLIC "-//Apple//DTD PLIST 1.0//EN" "http://www.apple.com/DTDs/PropertyList-1.0.dtd">
   528	<plist version="1.0">
   529	<dict>
   530	    <key>CFBundleName</key>
   531	    <string>Plow</string>
   532	    <key>CFBundleShortVersionString</key>
   533	    <string>0.1.0</string>
   534	    <key>CFBundleVersion</key>
   535	    <string>1</string>
   536	    <key>SUFeedURL</key>
   537	    <string>https://example.test/appcast.xml</string>
   538	    <key>SUPublicEDKey</key>
   539	    <string>test-public-key</string>
   540	</dict>
   541	</plist>
   542	""",
   543	        encoding="utf-8",
   544	    )
   545	    macos_binary.write_text("#!/bin/sh\nexit 0\n", encoding="utf-8")
   546	    macos_binary.chmod(0o755)
   547	    # python3 must be a real interpreter for plowd-validate-package's manifest check
   548	    python_bin = runtime_root / "python" / "bin" / "python3"
   549	    python_bin.parent.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
   550	    python_bin.symlink_to(sys.executable)

   587	    for file_path in required_files:
   588	        file_path.parent.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
   589	        file_path.write_text("placeholder")
   590	    # runtime-manifest.json is validated by plowd-validate-package
   591	    manifest_path = contents_root / "Resources" / "runtime-manifest.json"
   592	    manifest_path.parent.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
   593	    manifest_path.write_text(
   594	        '{"artifacts": [{"name": "openclaw", "version": "1.0", "url": "https://example.test/openclaw.tar.zst", "sha256": "abc", "size": 1, "gitRef": ""}, {"name": "camoufox", "version": "1.0", "url": "https://example.test/camoufox.tar.zst", "sha256": "bcd", "size": 1, "gitRef": ""}]}',
   595	        encoding="utf-8",
   596	    )

   598	
   599	def test_validate_package_rejects_bundle_missing_plowd_dist_info(tmp_path):
   600	    """A packaged runtime that exists structurally but lacks plowd-*.dist-info/
   601	    is the exact regression #478 shape: site-packages/ is present, all files
   602	    pass the existence check, but plowd dies at import with PackageNotFoundError
   603	    because importlib.metadata can't find the metadata."""
   604	    app_bundle = tmp_path / "Plow.app"
   605	    _create_minimal_valid_app_bundle(app_bundle)
   606	
   607	    # Sanity: the unmodified bundle passes validation.
   608	    ok = subprocess.run(
   609	        [str(VALIDATE_PACKAGE_SCRIPT), "--app-bundle", str(app_bundle), "--mode", "offline"],
   610	        capture_output=True,
   611	        text=True,
   612	    )
   613	    assert ok.returncode == 0, f"baseline bundle should validate cleanly, got: {ok.stderr}"
   614	
   615	    # Remove the dist-info; site-packages/ itself stays so this isn't caught
   616	    # by the existing required_runtime_paths loop.
   617	    dist_info = (
   618	        app_bundle / "Contents" / "Resources" / "runtime"
   619	        / "site-packages" / "plowd-0.1.1.dist-info"
   620	    )
   621	    import shutil
   622	    shutil.rmtree(dist_info)
   623	
   624	    fail = subprocess.run(
   625	        [str(VALIDATE_PACKAGE_SCRIPT), "--app-bundle", str(app_bundle), "--mode", "offline"],
   626	        capture_output=True,
   627	        text=True,
   628	    )
   629	    assert fail.returncode != 0, "validate-package must reject a bundle missing plowd dist-info"
   630	    assert "plowd-*.dist-info" in fail.stderr, (
   631	        f"error message should mention the missing dist-info; got stderr:\n{fail.stderr}"
   632	    )
   633	
   634	
   635	def test_validate_package_pins_plowd_dist_info_check():
   636	    """Static guard so a future deletion of the dist-info check in
   637	    plowd-validate-package surfaces here, not as a packaged-app crash."""
   638	    validate_script = VALIDATE_PACKAGE_SCRIPT.read_text(encoding="utf-8")
   639	    assert "plowd-*.dist-info/METADATA" in validate_script, (
   640	        "plowd-validate-package must check for plowd-*.dist-info/METADATA so "
   641	        "regression #478 can't ship as a structurally-valid-but-unbootable bundle"
   642	    )

   645	def test_stage_runtime_installs_plowd_dist_info():
   646	    """plowd's `importlib.metadata.version("plowd")` calls need `plowd-*.dist-info/`
   647	    on sys.path. The rsync of the source tree into `${stage_dir}/plowd` doesn't
   648	    include metadata, so plowd-stage-runtime must explicitly install plowd into
   649	    site-packages alongside the external deps so the dist-info is present.
   650	    Without this, packaged apps die at import with PackageNotFoundError before
   651	    binding the HTTP port (regression #478)."""
   652	    stage_script = (
   653	        REPO_ROOT / "app" / "plowd" / "scripts" / "plowd-stage-runtime"
   654	    ).read_text(encoding="utf-8")
   655	
   656	    # Whitespace-tolerant: pin the unique combination of flags that identifies
   657	    # the dist-info install (--no-deps + ${project_root}) without locking the
   658	    # script to a specific line-continuation/indent style.
   659	    assert re.search(
   660	        r'uv pip install\b[^\n]*'
   661	        r'(?:\\\s*\n[^\n]*)*'
   662	        r'--target\s+"\$\{stage_dir\}/site-packages"'
   663	        r'[^\n]*(?:\\\s*\n[^\n]*)*'
   664	        r'--no-deps'
   665	        r'[^\n]*(?:\\\s*\n[^\n]*)*'
   666	        r'"\$\{project_root\}"',
   667	        stage_script,
   668	    ), (
   669	        "plowd-stage-runtime must `uv pip install --no-deps` plowd into "
   670	        "${stage_dir}/site-packages so the daemon's importlib.metadata.version"
   671	        "('plowd') call resolves"
   672	    )
   673

   273	# that's the data partition's mount point on real hdiutil's tabular output
   274	# and a single-line stub's mount path under tests. Mirrors the parser in
   275	# plowd-verify-dmg.
   276	mounted_volume="$(printf '%s\n' "${attach_output}" | awk '$NF ~ /^\// { last=$NF } END { print last }')"
   277	[[ -n "${mounted_volume}" ]] || { echo "error: failed to determine mounted volume for ${output}" >&2; exit 1; }
   278	codesign --verify --deep --strict --verbose=4 "${mounted_volume}/Plow.app"
   279	hdiutil detach "${mounted_volume}" >/dev/null
   280	mounted_volume=""
   281	
   282	echo "submitting DMG to Apple notarization..."
   283	submit_output="$(xcrun notarytool submit "${output}" --keychain-profile "${notary_profile}" --wait --output-format json)"
   284	submit_id="$(python3 -c 'import json,sys; print(json.load(sys.stdin).get("id",""))' <<<"${submit_output}")"
   285	submit_status="$(python3 -c 'import json,sys; print(json.load(sys.stdin).get("status",""))' <<<"${submit_output}")"
   286	if [[ "${submit_status}" != "Accepted" ]]; then
   287	  echo "notarization failed with status: ${submit_status:-unknown}" >&2
   288	  if [[ -n "${submit_id}" ]]; then
   289	    echo "submission id: ${submit_id}" >&2
   290	    xcrun notarytool log "${submit_id}" --keychain-profile "${notary_profile}" || true
   291	  fi
   292	  exit 1
   293	fi
   294	echo "stapling notarization ticket..."
   295	xcrun stapler staple "${output}"
   296	echo "checking local Gatekeeper assessment for the DMG..."
   297	if ! spctl --assess --type open -vv "${output}"; then
   298	  echo "warning: local spctl assessment of the DMG failed; notarization was accepted and the ticket was stapled" >&2
   299	fi
   300	
   301	# PLO-29: verify the final shipping artifact has no custom volume icon and
   302	# that the volume name is "Plow" before it gets uploaded. This is mandatory:
   303	# any path that reaches the upload step has been verified.
   304	echo "verifying final DMG against PLO-29 contract..."
   305	"${repo_root}/app/plowd/scripts/plowd-verify-dmg" "${output}"
   306	
   307	echo "writing checksum..."
   308	shasum -a 256 "${output}" > "${output}.sha256"
   309	
   310	echo "signed distribution image created: ${output}"
   311	echo "sha256 file: ${output}.sha256"
   312	profile_args=()
   313	if [[ -n "${s3_profile}" ]]; then
   314	  profile_args=(--profile "${s3_profile}")
   315	fi
   316	
   317	echo "uploading versioned DMG artifacts to S3..."
   318	aws s3 cp "${output}" "s3://${s3_bucket}/${dmg_key}" ${profile_args[@]+"${profile_args[@]}"}
   319	aws s3 cp "${output}.sha256" "s3://${s3_bucket}/${dmg_sha_key}" ${profile_args[@]+"${profile_args[@]}"}

   235	# Mounts a writable scratch DMG with production staging, drops you into
   236	# Finder to arrange it, then captures the resulting .DS_Store into
   237	# app/plowd/dmg/.DS_Store. That checked-in .DS_Store is shipped verbatim
   238	# by plowd-beta-package-signed in CI; without re-running this recipe,
   239	# layout changes won't reach users. Use whenever you change
   240	# background.tiff, want to move icons, or need to resize the install
   241	# window.
   242	#
   243	# Workflow: arrange the Finder window, close it with Cmd-W (flushes
   244	# .DS_Store), then press Enter at the script's prompt. Defaults --app
   245	# to the release build, falling back to /Applications/Plow.app. See

From 4edb57969ae7e2863b328ba5055e5ce1511e9974 Mon Sep 17 00:00:00 2001
From: Swagat Patel <swagatpatel@users.noreply.github.com>
Date: Thu, 30 Apr 2026 18:20:56 -0700
Subject: [PATCH 1/9] PLO-29: drop custom DMG volume icon
MIME-Version: 1.0
Content-Type: text/plain; charset=UTF-8
Content-Transfer-Encoding: 8bit

Mounted Plow DMGs were showing the app icon, which Sam reported as
indistinguishable from the running app in Finder. Strip the custom
icon so the mounted volume uses the default macOS removable-volume
icon while keeping the volume name "Plow".

- plowd-beta-package-signed: stop staging .VolumeIcon.icns; create the
  ULFO DMG directly instead of going UDRW -> attach -> set
  kHasCustomIcon FinderInfo -> detach -> convert. The dance only
  existed to host the icon flag.
- delete the now-orphaned app/plowd/dmg/volume.icns asset.
- add plowd-verify-dmg + `just app dmg-verify` recipe: mounts a built
  DMG, asserts the volume name is "Plow" and that no .VolumeIcon.icns
  ships at the volume root. Smoke-tested locally on three paths
  (happy / .VolumeIcon present / wrong volname) — all behave.
- test_signed_package_script_builds_ulfo_dmg_without_staging_ds_store:
  pin the new contract (no .VolumeIcon.icns staged, no UDRW/convert).

Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.7 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>

+# Mount a Plow DMG and assert no custom volume icon ships at the root
+# (PLO-29). Thin alias for plowd-verify-dmg: with no argument the verifier
+# falls back to .build/Plow.dmg from the repo root.
+dmg-verify *dmg:
+    @plowd/scripts/plowd-verify-dmg {{dmg}}
+
+# Mounts a writable scratch DMG with production staging, drops you into
+# Finder to arrange it, then captures the resulting .DS_Store into
+# app/plowd/dmg/.DS_Store. That checked-in .DS_Store is shipped verbatim
+# by plowd-beta-package-signed in CI; without re-running this recipe,
+# layout changes won't reach users. Use whenever you change
+# background.tiff, want to move icons, or need to resize the install
+# window.
+#
+# Workflow: arrange the Finder window, close it with Cmd-W (flushes
+# .DS_Store), then press Enter at the script's prompt. Defaults --app
+# to the release build, falling back to /Applications/Plow.app. See
+# plowd/scripts/plowd-record-dmg-layout for shortcuts and caveats.
+#
+# Re-record the Finder window layout used by the release DMG.
+dmg-record-layout app="":
+    @if [[ -n "{{app}}" ]]; then \
+      plowd/scripts/plowd-record-dmg-layout --app "{{app}}"; \
+    else \
+      plowd/scripts/plowd-record-dmg-layout; \
+    fi
+

 runtime action="" profile="${PLOW_RELEASES_PROFILE-plow}" prefix="runtime":
     @\
     s3_bucket="releases.plow.co"; \
     s3_prefix="{{prefix}}"; \
     case "{{action}}" in \
       manifest) \
         uv run --project plowd python scripts/generate-runtime-manifest.py --vm-manifest vm/manifest.toml --bucket "$s3_bucket" --prefix "$s3_prefix" --images-output Phoenix/Resources/runtime-images-manifest.json ;; \
       build) \
         S3_BUCKET="$s3_bucket" S3_PREFIX="$s3_prefix" scripts/build-container-images.sh ;; \
       deploy) \
         S3_BUCKET="$s3_bucket" S3_PREFIX="$s3_prefix" AWS_PROFILE="{{profile}}" scripts/upload-runtime-artifacts.sh && \
         uv run --project plowd python scripts/generate-runtime-manifest.py --vm-manifest vm/manifest.toml --bucket "$s3_bucket" --prefix "$s3_prefix" --images-output Phoenix/Resources/runtime-images-manifest.json ;; \
       ""|help|-h|--help) \
         echo "Usage: just runtime <manifest|build|deploy> [profile=...] [prefix=...]" ;; \
       *) \
         echo "error: unknown runtime action '{{action}}' (expected: manifest|build|deploy)" >&2; exit 1 ;; \
     esac
 
 [private]
 vm-reset variant="" bundle_id="co.plow.app.dev":
     @effective_variant="{{variant}}"; \
     if [[ "$effective_variant" == variant=* ]]; then \
       effective_variant="${effective_variant#variant=}"; \
     fi; \
     variant_id="$(printf '%s' "$effective_variant" | tr '[:upper:]' '[:lower:]' | sed -E 's/[^a-z0-9]+/./g; s/^\.+//; s/\.+$//; s/\.\.+/./g')"; \
     effective_bundle_id="{{bundle_id}}"; \
     if [[ -n "$variant_id" ]]; then effective_bundle_id="${effective_bundle_id}.${variant_id}"; fi; \
     runtime_vm_dir="${HOME}/Library/Application Support/${effective_bundle_id}/vm"; \
     lima_home_dir="${HOME}/.plow/${effective_bundle_id}/lima"; \
     lima_instance="plow-runtime"; \
     bundled_limactl="$(pwd)/Phoenix/Resources/bin/limactl"; \
     if [[ -x "$bundled_limactl" ]]; then \
       limactl_bin="$bundled_limactl"; \
     elif limactl_on_path="$(command -v limactl 2>/dev/null)"; then \
       limactl_bin="$limactl_on_path"; \
     else \
       printf '%s\n' \
         "error: limactl is required for just vm-reset but was not found." \
         "  Bundled path checked: $bundled_limactl" \
         "" \
         "Stage the pinned bundled binary with:" \
         "  just fetch-limactl" \
         "  (or: cd app && just fetch-limactl)" \
         "" \
         "If you also want a system limactl on PATH:" \
         "  brew install lima" >&2; \
       exit 1; \
     fi; \
     if [[ -d "$lima_home_dir" ]]; then \
       LIMA_HOME="$lima_home_dir" "$limactl_bin" delete --force "$lima_instance" >/dev/null 2>&1 || true; \
     fi; \
     rm -rf "$runtime_vm_dir" "$lima_home_dir"; \
     echo "Reset Lima runtime state: $runtime_vm_dir + $lima_home_dir ($lima_instance)"
 
 # `setopt no_nomatch` lets callers pass literal globs (e.g. systemctl unit patterns)
 # through to the guest without zsh failing on unmatched host-side globs.
 #
 # Run the bundled (or PATH) limactl against the current variant's Lima home.
 limactl *args:
     @setopt no_nomatch; \
